Only the topmost non-zero field is used.\n89: \n90: \t// Quantity is a quantity associated with the signal that is evaluated against the specified operator.\n91: \tQuantity *resource.Quantity\n92: \t// Percentage represents the usage percentage over the total resource that is evaluated against the specified operator.\n93: \tPercentage float32\n94: }\n95: \n96: // Threshold defines a metric for when eviction should occur.\n97: type Threshold struct {\n98: \t// Signal defines the entity that was measured.\n99: \tSignal Signal\n100: \t// Operator represents a relationship of a signal to a value.\n101: \tOperator ThresholdOperator\n102: \t// Value is the threshold the resource is evaluated against.\n103: \tValue ThresholdValue\n104: \t// GracePeriod represents the amount of time that a threshold must be met before eviction is triggered.\n105: \tGracePeriod time.Duration\n106: \t// MinReclaim represents the minimum amount of resource to reclaim if the threshold is met.\n107: \tMinReclaim *ThresholdValue\n108: }\n109: \n110: // GetThresholdQuantity returns the expected quantity value for a thresholdValue\n111: func GetThresholdQuantity(value ThresholdValue, capacity *resource.Quantity) *resource.Quantity {\n112: \tif value.Quantity != nil {\n113: \t\tres := value.Quantity.DeepCopy()\n114: \t\treturn &res\n115: \t}\n116: \treturn resource.NewQuantity(int64(float64(capacity.Value())*float64(value.Percentage)), resource.BinarySI)\n117: }\n118: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0@d17b464c6fcd3273e4b1f695890bf0af7d5b272d/-/blob/pkg/kubelet/eviction/api/types.go"}}}

system on memory pressure is implemented primarily in the kubelet's eviction package. Here's how it works:\\n\\n**Threshold Definition:**\\nMemory pressure eviction thresholds are defined in platform-specific files:\\n- `pkg/kubelet/eviction/defaults_linux.go` and `defaults_others.go` define DefaultEvictionHard with a default memory.available threshold of 100Mi\\n- `pkg/kubelet/eviction/defaults_windows.go` defines DefaultEvictionHard with a default memory.available threshold of 500Mi\\n- `pkg/kubelet/eviction/api/types.go` defines the signal types: SignalMemoryAvailable (\\\"memory.available\\\") and SignalAllocatableMemoryAvailable (\\\"allocatableMemory.available\\\")\\n\\n**Eviction Manager Implementation:**\\n`pkg/kubelet/eviction/eviction_manager.go` contains the managerImpl struct, which is the main eviction manager. The critical method is:\\n- `synchronize()` (lines 241-440): The main control loop that periodically monitors resource usage and triggers pod eviction. It:\\n  1. Calls makeSignalObservations() to collect current memory stats from the node\\n  2. Calls thresholdsMet() to check if memory pressure thresholds have been crossed\\n  3. Ranks pods using rankMemoryPressure() if thresholds are met\\n  4. Evicts the highest-priority pod by calling evictPod()\\n- `IsUnderMemoryPressure()` (lines 220-225): Returns true if the node is under memory pressure\\n- `Admit()` (lines 145-181): Admission handler that rejects BestEffort pods during memory pressure (except those with proper tolerations)\\n\\n**Signal Observation & Threshold Checking:**\\n`pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers.go` contains:\\n- `makeSignalObservations()` (lines 839-920): Creates observations of current memory availability by reading from the node's memory stats. It calls makeMemoryAvailableSignalObservation() to get platform-specific memory measurements.\\n- `thresholdsMet()` (lines 933-960): Determines which thresholds have been crossed by comparing available memory against configured thresholds using the operator (OpLessThan for memory)\\n- `rankMemoryPressure()` (lines 807-812): Ranks pods for eviction by: (1) whether usage exceeds requests, (2) priority, (3) memory usage above requests. This ensures BestEffort pods and pods exceeding their requests are evicted first.\\n\\n**Platform-Specific Memory Signal Creation:**\\n- `pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers_others.go` (non-Windows): `makeMemoryAvailableSignalObservation()` creates memory signal observations from summary.Node.Memory.AvailableBytes and WorkingSetBytes\\n- `pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers_windows.go` (Windows): Similar platform-specific implementation with Windows-specific memory calculations\\n\\n**Signal-to-Condition Mapping:**\\nIn `pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers.go` (init function, lines 75-99), eviction signals are mapped to node conditions:\\n- SignalMemoryAvailable and SignalAllocatableMemoryAvailable both map to NodeMemoryPressure\\nThis allows the eviction manager to set the NodeMemoryPressure condition when memory thresholds are crossed.\\n\\n**Complete Eviction Flow:**\\n1. kubelet calls evictionManager.Start() which starts the control loop\\n2. Periodically, synchronize() is called\\n3. Current memory stats are collected via makeSignalObservations()\\n4. thresholdsMet() checks if memory.available < configured threshold (default 100Mi on Linux)\\n5. Calls makeSignalObservations() to collect current memory stats from the node\\n  2. Calls thresholdsMet() to check if memory pressure thresholds have been crossed\\n  3. It calls makeMemoryAvailableSignalObservation() to get platform-specific memory measurements.\\n- `thresholdsMet()` (lines 933-960): Determines which thresholds have been crossed by comparing available memory against configured thresholds using the operator (OpLessThan for memory)\\n- `rankMemoryPressure()` (lines 807-812): Ranks pods for eviction by: (1) whether usage exceeds requests, (2) priority, (3) memory usage above requests. This ensures BestEffort pods and pods exceeding their requests are evicted first.\\n\\n**Platform-Specific Memory Signal Creation:**\\n- `pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers_others.go` (non-Windows): `makeMemoryAvailableSignalObservation()` creates memory signal observations from summary.Node.Memory.AvailableBytes and WorkingSetBytes\\n- `pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers_windows.go` (Windows): Similar platform-specific implementation with Windows-specific memory calculations\\n\\n**Signal-to-Condition Mapping:**\\nIn `pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers.go` (init function, lines 75-99), eviction signals are mapped to node conditions:\\n- SignalMemoryAvailable and SignalAllocatableMemoryAvailable both map to NodeMemoryPressure\\nThis allows the eviction manager to set the NodeMemoryPressure condition when memory thresholds are crossed.\\n\\n**Complete Eviction Flow:**\\n1. kubelet calls evictionManager.Start() which starts the control loop\\n2. Current memory stats are collected via makeSignalObservations()\\n4. thresholdsMet() checks if memory.available < configured threshold (default 100Mi on Linux)\\n5.
